## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# big-code-kafka-sec-001: Kafka SASL Authentication Flow Security Analysis

## Task

Trace the Apache Kafka SASL authentication flow from channel creation through mechanism negotiation (PLAIN, SCRAM-SHA-256, OAUTHBEARER, GSSAPI), the challenge-response exchange, principal extraction, to ACL-based authorization. Identify all entry points where untrusted client data enters the SASL subsystem, map the data flow through each authentication mechanism, and analyze the security properties of the authentication and authorization chain.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 (mirror of apache/kafka) (Java, ~1.2M LOC)
- **Category**: Security Analysis
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/security/` (authenticator, plain, scram, oauthbearer packages) and `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/` (channel builders)

## Requirements

1. Identify all entry points where untrusted data enters the SASL subsystem (client connections, SASL tokens, handshake requests)
2. Trace the channel builder architecture: how `ChannelBuilders` creates `SaslChannelBuilder` which wires up `SaslServerAuthenticator`
3. Map the SASL handshake protocol: `ApiVersionsRequest` -> `SaslHandshakeRequest` -> mechanism-specific exchange -> authenticated principal
4. Trace at least two mechanism implementations (PLAIN and SCRAM) through their callback handlers to credential verification
5. Identify how `KafkaPrincipal` is extracted post-authentication and how `Authorizer.authorize()` enforces ACLs
6. Document existing mitigations and where they may be insufficient

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file.ext — role in attack surface
...

## Entry Points
1. path/to/entry.ext:function_name — accepts [type of untrusted input]
...

## Data Flow
### Flow 1: [name]
1. Source: path/to/source.ext (untrusted input enters here)
2. Transform: path/to/transform.ext (data is [processed/validated/not validated])
3. Sink: path/to/sink.ext (sensitive operation: [db query/file write/exec/etc.])

## Dependency Chain
[Ordered list of files from entry to sink]

## Analysis
[Detailed security analysis including:
- Vulnerability class (injection, auth bypass, SSRF, etc.)
- Existing mitigations and their gaps
- Attack scenarios
- Recommended remediation]

## Summary
[Concise description of the vulnerability and its impact]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Attack surface coverage: Did you identify all files in the SASL authentication data flow?
- Entry point identification: Did you find the correct entry points (channel builders, authenticators)?
- Data flow completeness: Did you trace the full path from connection to authorized principal?
- Analysis quality: Is the SASL mechanism architecture correctly described?

372026-03-11T17:53:10.775094agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a thorough understanding of the Kafka SASL authentication flow. Let me organize my findings before writing the solution:

## Key findings:

### 1. Channel Builder Architecture
- `ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()` is the entry point for creating server-side channel builders
- For SASL_PLAINTEXT or SASL_SSL, it creates a `SaslChannelBuilder`
- `SaslChannelBuilder.configure()` sets up:
  - `createServerCallbackHandlers()` - creates mechanism-specific callback handlers
  - Per-mechanism: PLAIN → `PlainServerCallbackHandler`, SCRAM → `ScramServerCallbackHandler`, OAUTHBEARER → `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, GSSAPI → `SaslServerCallbackHandler`
  - Login managers and JAAS subjects per mechanism
- `SaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()` calls `buildServerAuthenticator()` → `SaslServerAuthenticator`

### 2. SASL Handshake Protocol (State Machine in SaslServerAuthenticator)
States:
- `INITIAL_REQUEST` → `HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST`
- `HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST` (ApiVersions or Handshake)
- `HANDSHAKE_REQUEST` (after ApiVersions, must get Handshake)
- `AUTHENTICATE` (mechanism-specific exchange)
- `COMPLETE` or `FAILED`

Flow:
1. Client sends raw TCP bytes
2. `authenticate()` reads bytes into `NetworkReceive` buffer (bounded by `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` = `BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE`)
3. Dispatches to `handleKafkaRequest()` or `handleSaslToken()`
4. `handleKafkaRequest()` parses `RequestHeader`, validates API key is `API_VERSIONS` or `SASL_HANDSHAKE`
5. `handleHandshakeRequest()` extracts `clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism()` (untrusted input)
6. Validates mechanism is in `enabledMechanisms` list
7. Creates `SaslServer` via `createSaslServer(clientMechanism)`
8. Transiti
... (truncated)

*/\\n108:     private enum SaslState {\\n109:         INITIAL_REQUEST,               // May be SaslHandshake or ApiVersions for authentication\\n110:         HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST, // May be authenticate() throws IOException {\\n251:         if (saslState != SaslState.REAUTH_PROCESS_HANDSHAKE) {\\n252:             if (netOutBuffer != null && }\\n500:     }\\n501: \\n502:     /**\\n503:      * @throws InvalidRequestException if the request is not in Kafka format or if the API key is invalid. Optional.of(clientPort()),\\n521:                     KafkaPrincipal.ANONYMOUS, listenerName, securityProtocol, ClientInformation.EMPTY, false);\\n522:             RequestAndSize requestAndSize = invalid.\\n540:                 // If it's the initial request, this could be an ancient client (see method documentation for more details),\\n541:                 // a client configured with the wrong security protocol or a non kafka-client altogether (eg http client).\\n542:                 throw new InvalidRequestException(\\\"Invalid request, potential reasons: kafka client configured with }\\n547:     }\\n548: \\n549:     private String handleHandshakeRequest(RequestContext context, SaslHandshakeRequest handshakeRequest) throws IOException, UnsupportedSaslMechanismException {\\n550: {
  "thought": "Now I have a thorough understanding of the Kafka SASL authentication flow. Let me organize my findings before writing the solution:\n\n## Key findings:\n\n### 1. Channel Builder Architecture\n- `ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()` is the entry point for creating server-side channel builders\n- For SASL_PLAINTEXT or SASL_SSL, it creates a `SaslChannelBuilder`\n- `SaslChannelBuilder.configure()` sets up:\n  - `createServerCallbackHandlers()` - creates mechanism-specific callback handlers\n  - Per-mechanism: PLAIN \u2192 `PlainServerCallbackHandler`, SCRAM \u2192 `ScramServerCallbackHandler`, OAUTHBEARER \u2192 `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`, GSSAPI \u2192 `SaslServerCallbackHandler`\n  - Login managers and JAAS subjects per mechanism\n- `SaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()` calls `buildServerAuthenticator()` \u2192 `SaslServerAuthenticator`\n\n### 2. SASL Handshake Protocol (State Machine in SaslServerAuthenticator)\nStates:\n- `INITIAL_REQUEST` \u2192 `HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST`\n- `HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST` (ApiVersions or Handshake)\n- `HANDSHAKE_REQUEST` (after ApiVersions, must get Handshake)\n- `AUTHENTICATE` (mechanism-specific exchange)\n- `COMPLETE` or `FAILED`\n\nFlow:\n1. Client sends raw TCP bytes\n2. `authenticate()` reads bytes into `NetworkReceive` buffer (bounded by `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` = `BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE`)\n3. Dispatches to `handleKafkaRequest()` or `handleSaslToken()`\n4. `handleKafkaRequest()` parses `RequestHeader`, validates API key is `API_VERSIONS` or `SASL_HANDSHAKE`\n5. `handleHandshakeRequest()` extracts `clientMechanism = handshakeRequest.data().mechanism()` (untrusted input)\n6. Validates mechanism is in `enabledMechanisms` list\n7. Creates `SaslServer` via `createSaslServer(clientMechanism)`\n8. Transitions to `AUTHENTICATE` state\n9. `handleSaslToken()` passes bytes to `saslServer.evaluateResponse(authBytes)`\n\n### 3. PLAIN Mechanism (PlainSaslServer)\nEntry point: `evaluateResponse(byte[] responseBytes)` in `PlainSaslServer`\n- Decodes bytes as UTF-8 string\n- Splits by NUL byte into [authzid, username, password]\n- Validates empty username and password\n- Creates `NameCallback(username)` and `PlainAuthenticateCallback(password)`\n- Calls `callbackHandler.handle()` \u2192 `PlainServerCallbackHandler.handle()`\n- `PlainServerCallbackHandler.authenticate()`:\n  - Looks up `user_<username>` in JAAS config entries (static config in JAAS)\n  - Returns `Utils.isEqualConstantTime(password, expectedPassword.toCharArray())`\n- If authentication fails: throws `SaslAuthenticationException` with \"Invalid username or password\"\n- Sets `this.authorizationId = username` on success\n\nSecurity note for PLAIN:\n- Username is from untrusted client input and used as a key into JAAS config lookup: `JAAS_USER_PREFIX + username` = `\"user_\" + username`. This is a map key lookup, so not vulnerable to injection per se, but it IS the identity of the principal.\n- Constant-time comparison used (good mitigation)\n- `authorizationId` is set directly to the client-supplied username\n\n### 4. SCRAM Mechanism (ScramSaslServer)\nEntry point: `evaluateResponse(byte[] response)` in `ScramSaslServer`\n- Phase 1: `RECEIVE_CLIENT_FIRST_MESSAGE`\n  - Parses `ClientFirstMessage(response)` using regex pattern\n  - Extracts `saslName`, `nonce`, `authorizationId`, `extensions`\n  - Converts saslName to username via `ScramFormatter.username(saslName)` (handles =2C \u2192 comma, =3D \u2192 =)\n  - Issues `NameCallback` + `ScramCredentialCallback` (or `DelegationTokenCredentialCallback` if token auth)\n  - `ScramServerCallbackHandler.handle()` looks up `credentialCache.get(username)` by the username from the client\n  - Returns `ServerFirstMessage` with server nonce + salt + iterations\n- Phase 2: `RECEIVE_CLIENT_FINAL_MESSAGE`\n  - Parses `ClientFinalMessage(response)`\n  - Validates nonce matches (server's previously generated nonce)\n  - Calls `verifyClientProof(clientFinalMessage)` using `MessageDigest.isEqual()` (constant-time)\n  - Sends `ServerFinalMessage` with server signature\n\nSecurity note for SCRAM:\n- Nonce verification ensures replay prevention\n- `MessageDigest.isEqual()` is constant-time for proof comparison\n- Username from client is used directly to look up credentials from cache\n\n### 5. OAUTHBEARER Mechanism (OAuthBearerSaslServer)\n- `evaluateResponse()` parses `OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse(response)`\n- Extracts token value, authorizationId, extensions\n- Calls `callbackHandler` with `OAuthBearerValidatorCallback` containing the JWT string\n- Validator (e.g., `OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler`) validates JWT signature, expiry, issuer, audience\n\n### 6. GSSAPI/Kerberos (SaslServerCallbackHandler)\n- Uses JVM's SASL GSSAPI implementation\n- Kerberos ticket validation done by GSSAPI\n- Principal extracted via `KerberosShortNamer` from the ticket's full name\n\n### 7. KafkaPrincipal Extraction\nAfter `saslServer.isComplete()`:\n- `SaslServerAuthenticator.principal()`:\n  - Creates `SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, securityProtocol, clientAddress, listenerName, sslSession)`\n  - Calls `principalBuilder.build(context)`\n- `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build()`:\n  - For SASL (non-GSSAPI): `new KafkaPrincipal(KafkaPrincipal.USER_TYPE, saslServer.getAuthorizationID())`\n  - `getAuthorizationID()` returns the username set during SASL exchange\n  - For GSSAPI: applies Kerberos short name transformation\n- The principal name IS the username/identity from the SASL mechanism's `getAuthorizationID()`\n\n### 8. Authorization\n- `Authorizer.authorize(AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext, List<Action> actions)` is called per-request\n- `requestContext.principal()` returns the `KafkaPrincipal` built post-authentication\n- `StandardAuthorizerData.authorize()` matches principal against ACL entries\n- ACL wildcards: `User:*`\n\n### 9. Entry Points (Untrusted Data)\n1. `SaslServerAuthenticator.authenticate()` - raw bytes from transport layer (line 264: `netInBuffer.readFrom(transportLayer)`)\n2. `handleKafkaRequest()` - parses mechanism name from `SaslHandshakeRequest` (line 550: `handshakeRequest.data().mechanism()`)\n3. `handleSaslToken()` - raw auth bytes passed to `saslServer.evaluateResponse(authBytes)` (line 461-462)\n4. `PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` - UTF-8 decoded response contains authzid/username/password\n5. `ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` - parsed SCRAM messages with client nonce and username\n6. `OAuthBearerSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` - raw JWT token\n\n### 10. Security Properties and Gaps\n\n**Existing Mitigations:**\n1. Size-bounded input: `saslAuthRequestMaxReceiveSize` (default from `BrokerSecurityConfigs.DEFAULT_SASL_SERVER_MAX_RECEIVE_SIZE`)\n2. Constant-time comparison: `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` for PLAIN passwords\n3. Constant-time comparison: `MessageDigest.isEqual()` for SCRAM proofs\n4. Mechanism whitelist: `handleHandshakeRequest()` validates client mechanism against `enabledMechanisms`\n5. Error message sanitization: SaslException details NOT sent to client (line 487-497 in SaslServerAuthenticator)\n6. Re-authentication principal pinning: `reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged()` prevents principal change during re-auth\n7. SCRAM nonce verification prevents replay attacks\n8. SCRAM uses server-side stored keys (not plaintext passwords in cache)\n9. SASL_SSL can layer mutual TLS + SASL\n\n**Potential Gaps/Weaknesses:**\n\n1. **PLAIN over SASL_PLAINTEXT**: PLAIN sends password in clear over the wire. If deployed without SSL, credentials are exposed. The code itself doesn't prevent this deployment.\n\n2. **PLAIN stores credentials in JAAS config**: `PlainServerCallbackHandler` looks up passwords from static JAAS config. This means broker restarts are required to update passwords. Also, passwords are in config files (can be read by anyone with file access).\n\n3. **Username enumeration via timing differences**: While the password comparison is constant-time (`Utils.isEqualConstantTime`), the `JAAS config lookup` itself may fail-fast if the username doesn't exist (returns `null` immediately for invalid usernames vs. comparing for valid ones). However, `authenticate()` returns `false` for null username anyway. More subtly: `expectedPassword = JaasContext.configEntryOption(...)` - if username doesn't exist, `expectedPassword` is null, and the method returns `false` early without doing the constant-time comparison. This creates a timing side channel that could enumerate valid usernames.\n\n4. **Authorization ID (authzid) flexibility in PLAIN**: The `authorizationId` in PLAIN defaults to username but the `authorizationIdFromClient` could differ if the client sends it. The code throws if `!authorizationIdFromClient.isEmpty() && !authorizationIdFromClient.equals(username)`. This means authzid must match username exactly - prevents impersonation.\n\n5. **No brute-force protection**: No rate limiting, account lockout, or IP blocking in the SASL code. A client can retry authentication indefinitely.\n\n6. **SCRAM iteration count check**: The code verifies `scramCredential.iterations() < mechanism.minIterations()` which protects against weak iteration counts in stored credentials.\n\n7. **OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler as default**: In `SaslChannelBuilder.createServerCallbackHandlers()`, OAUTHBEARER defaults to `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` which does NOT perform real JWT validation (it's the \"unsecured\" variant). This is a significant security gap for production use.\n\n8. **Custom KafkaPrincipalBuilder trust**: The `PRINCIPAL_BUILDER_CLASS_CONFIG` allows operators to plug in custom principal builders - if a buggy implementation is used, the principal may be set incorrectly.\n\n9. **SASL without authorization (no ACLs)**: If no `authorizer.class.name` is configured, `Authorizer.authorize()` is never called and there's no access control enforcement. Authentication succeeds but authorization is entirely absent.\n\n10. **`SaslAuthenticationException` message leakage in PLAIN**: `PlainSaslServer` throws `SaslAuthenticationException` with detail messages like \"Authentication failed: username not specified\" or \"Authentication failed: Invalid username or password\". These specific messages (thrown as `SaslAuthenticationException`) ARE sent to the client per the code comment, which could leak information (different errors for username vs. password issues could aid attack).\n\nWait, let me re-examine this. Looking at `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken()` (lines 474-498):\n- `SaslAuthenticationException` is caught and its `getMessage()` IS included in the response sent to clients\n- `SaslException` (non-authentication) - the error message is NOT included\n- So `PlainSaslServer` throwing `SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid username or password\")` would be sent to clients\n\nBut looking at PlainSaslServer more carefully:\n- `SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: username not specified\")` - sent to client \n- `SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: password not specified\")` - sent to client\n- `SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Invalid username or password\")` - sent to client\n- `SaslAuthenticationException(\"Authentication failed: Client requested an authorization id that is different from username\")` - sent to client\n\nThe first two could be useful to an attacker (differentiates \"no username\" vs \"wrong password\" cases), but the third is consistent.\n\n11. **SCRAM ClientFirstMessage error logging**: In `ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()`, `SaslException(\"Token Authentication failed: Invalid tokenId : \" + username)` is thrown, which includes the token ID from the client in the exception. However, the exception type is `SaslException` not `SaslAuthenticationException`, so it won't be sent to the client.\n\nActually wait, let me re-read. At line 141-144:\n```java\n} catch (SaslException | AuthenticationException e) {\n    throw e;\n} catch (Throwable e) {\n    throw new SaslException(\"Authentication failed: Credentials could not be obtained\", e);\n}\n```\nThe `SaslException` is re-thrown. In `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken()` at lines 481-497:\n- `SaslException` (non-Kerberos retriable) \u2192 sends generic error message without exception details\n\nSo `ScramSaslServer` is more careful. PLAIN is the one with the more specific error messages.\n\n### Summary for analysis:\n\nThe SASL authentication flow is well-structured and follows security best practices in most areas. The main attack surface issues are:\n\n1. **Cleartext credential exposure in PLAIN**: Credentials transmitted in plaintext when SASL_PLAINTEXT is used\n2. **Username timing oracle in PLAIN**: Non-constant-time behavior when username doesn't exist\n3. **No brute-force protection**: No rate limiting at the SASL layer\n4. **Default unsecured OAUTHBEARER**: The default OAuthBearer callback handler doesn't validate JWTs\n5. **No mandatory authz**: Authorization is optional and defaults to allow-all\n6. **Information leakage in PLAIN exceptions**: Some error details sent to client\n\nLet me now write the comprehensive solution.md file.\n"
}

[SaslServerAuthenticator.java:549]\n      \u2192 mechanism validated against enabledMechanisms\n  \u2192 createSaslServer(mechanism)                           [SaslServerAuthenticator.java:200]\n      PLAIN:  Sasl.createSaslServer() \u2192 PlainSaslServer   [PlainSaslServer.java]\n      SCRAM:  Sasl.createSaslServer() \u2192 ScramSaslServer   [ScramSaslServer.java]\n      OAUTH:  Sasl.createSaslServer() \u2192 OAuthBearerSaslServer [OAuthBearerSaslServer.java]\n      GSSAPI: createSaslKerberosServer()                  [SaslServerAuthenticator.java:219]\n  \u2192 handleSaslToken(clientToken)                          [SaslServerAuthenticator.java:421]\n      \u2192 saslServer.evaluateResponse(authBytes)\n          PLAIN: PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()        [PlainSaslServer.java:71]\n                 \u2192 extractTokens() \u2192 username/password\n                 \u2192 callbackHandler.handle()\n                 \u2192 PlainServerCallbackHandler.authenticate() [PlainServerCallbackHandler.java:61]\n                     \u2192 JaasContext.configEntryOption(\"user_\"+username)\n                     \u2192 Utils.isEqualConstantTime()\n          SCRAM: ScramSaslServer.evaluateResponse()         [ScramSaslServer.java:96]\n                 \u2192 ClientFirstMessage(bytes) / ClientFinalMessage(bytes)\n                 \u2192 callbackHandler.handle()\n                 \u2192 ScramServerCallbackHandler.handle()      [ScramServerCallbackHandler.java:53]\n                     \u2192 credentialCache.get(username)\n                 \u2192 verifyClientProof() \u2192 MessageDigest.isEqual()\n          OAUTH: OAuthBearerSaslServer.evaluateResponse()  [OAuthBearerSaslServer.java:86]\n                 \u2192 OAuthBearerClientInitialResponse(bytes)\n                 \u2192 OAuthBearerValidatorCallback (or Unsecured)\n  \u2192 saslServer.isComplete() == true\n  \u2192 SaslServerAuthenticator.principal()                   [SaslServerAuthenticator.java:307]\n      \u2192 SaslAuthenticationContext(saslServer, ...)\n      \u2192 DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build(context)       [DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.java:69]\n          \u2192 new KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", saslServer.getAuthorizationID())\n  \u2192 KafkaChannel authenticated; KafkaPrincipal set on session\n  \u2192 Per-request: Authorizer.authorize(requestContext, actions) [Authorizer.java:107]\n      requestContext.principal() == KafkaPrincipal from above\n      \u2192 StandardAuthorizerData.authorize()                [StandardAuthorizerData.java:228]\n          \u2192 matchingPrincipals() \u2192 ACL lookup\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### 1. Channel Builder Architecture\n\n`ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()` is called once per listener at broker startup. For `SASL_PLAINTEXT` or `SASL_SSL`, it:\n\n1. Reads enabled mechanisms from `sasl.enabled.mechanisms` broker config\n2. Loads a `JaasContext` per mechanism (from `sasl.<listener>.jaas.config` or the JVM-level `java.security.auth.login.config`)\n3. Constructs `SaslChannelBuilder(connectionMode=SERVER, jaasContexts, ...)`\n4. `SaslChannelBuilder.configure()` calls `createServerCallbackHandlers()` which instantiates:\n   - `PlainServerCallbackHandler` for PLAIN\n   - `ScramServerCallbackHandler(credentialCache, tokenCache)` for SCRAM variants\n   - `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` as the *default* for OAUTHBEARER (can be overridden via `listener.name.<name>.oauthbearer.sasl.server.callback.handler.class`)\n   - `SaslServerCallbackHandler` for GSSAPI and others\n5. On each new TCP connection, `SaslChannelBuilder.buildChannel()` creates a new `KafkaChannel` with a lazily-created `SaslServerAuthenticator`\n\n### 2. SASL Handshake Protocol State Machine\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator` implements a strict state machine:\n\n```\nINITIAL_REQUEST\n  \u2192 [ApiVersionsRequest received]  \u2192 HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST \u2192 HANDSHAKE_REQUEST\n  \u2192 [SaslHandshakeRequest received] \u2192 HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST (then immediately)\nHANDSHAKE_REQUEST / HANDSHAKE_OR_VERSIONS_REQUEST\n  \u2192 [SaslHandshakeRequest received] \u2192 validate mechanism \u2192 createSaslServer \u2192 AUTHENTICATE\nAUTHENTICATE\n  \u2192 [SASL tokens] \u2192 saslServer.evaluateResponse() (multiple rounds possible)\n  \u2192 [isComplete()] \u2192 COMPLETE\nFAILED (terminal)\n```\n\nThe state machine prevents protocol state confusion: receiving a `SASL_AUTHENTICATE` before completing the handshake or after authentication completes throws `IllegalSaslStateException`. Only `API_VERSIONS` and `SASL_HANDSHAKE` API keys are accepted before authentication (`handleKafkaRequest()` L515\u2013516).\n\n### 3. Vulnerability Class: Timing Oracle on PLAIN Username Existence\n\n**Location**: `PlainServerCallbackHandler.java:authenticate()` (L61\u201369)\n\n```java\nprotected boolean authenticate(String username, char[] password) throws IOException {\n    if (username == null)\n        return false;\n    else {\n        String expectedPassword = JaasContext.configEntryOption(jaasConfigEntries,\n                JAAS_USER_PREFIX + username,\n                PlainLoginModule.class.getName());\n        return expectedPassword != null && Utils.isEqualConstantTime(password, expectedPassword.toCharArray());\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhen `username` is valid, `expectedPassword` is non-null and `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` runs (O(password-length) time). When `username` is invalid, `expectedPassword` is null and the function returns `false` immediately without calling `isEqualConstantTime()`. This creates a measurable timing difference between valid and invalid usernames. An attacker can enumerate valid usernames by measuring response time.\n\n**Severity**: Medium \u2014 enables offline username enumeration without credentials. Particularly relevant when combined with no brute-force protection.\n\n**Mitigation gap**: `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` was correctly applied for the password comparison, but the early-exit path for missing users was not addressed.\n\n### 4. Vulnerability Class: Cleartext Credential Transmission (PLAIN)\n\n**Location**: `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (L85)\n\nSASL/PLAIN transmits credentials as `\\0username\\0password` in a single message, with no cryptographic protection at the SASL layer. If deployed as `SASL_PLAINTEXT` (no TLS), credentials are exposed to any network observer. The code does nothing to detect or prevent this insecure deployment.\n\n**Severity**: Critical when `SASL_PLAINTEXT` is used; mitigated when `SASL_SSL` is used.\n\n### 5. Vulnerability Class: Default Insecure OAUTHBEARER Validator\n\n**Location**: `SaslChannelBuilder.java:createServerCallbackHandlers()` (L330\u2013331)\n\n```java\nelse if (mechanism.equals(OAuthBearerLoginModule.OAUTHBEARER_MECHANISM))\n    callbackHandler = new OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler();\n```\n\nWhen no explicit `sasl.server.callback.handler.class` is configured for OAUTHBEARER, the broker uses `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler`. This handler accepts any syntactically valid JWT without verifying its cryptographic signature, expiry, issuer, or audience. Any client presenting a self-crafted JWT with any `sub` claim can authenticate as any user identity.\n\n**Severity**: Critical \u2014 complete authentication bypass for OAUTHBEARER in the default configuration.\n\n**Mitigation**: Deploy `OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler` and configure `sasl.oauthbearer.jwks.endpoint.url`.\n\n### 6. Vulnerability Class: No Brute-Force Protection\n\nThe SASL layer applies no rate limiting, account lockout, or connection throttling. `SaslServerAuthenticator` resets its state to `FAILED` on each failure but does not track failure counts. A client can open a new TCP connection per attempt and attempt unlimited credential guessing against PLAIN or SCRAM.\n\n**Severity**: Medium \u2014 allows offline and online brute-force attacks.\n\n### 7. Vulnerability Class: Authorization Optional / Not Enforced\n\n**Location**: `Authorizer.java` \u2014 pluggable interface\n\nIf `authorizer.class.name` is not set in broker configuration, no `Authorizer` instance is created and `Authorizer.authorize()` is never called. Successfully authenticated clients have unrestricted access to all topics and APIs. The authentication layer does not enforce that authorization is configured.\n\n**Severity**: High in environments where the broker is mistakenly deployed without ACLs but with authentication.\n\n### 8. Information Leakage via SaslAuthenticationException in PLAIN\n\n**Location**: `PlainSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (L91\u201396), `SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (L474\u2013480)\n\n`SaslAuthenticationException` is a subclass of `AuthenticationException`. Looking at `SaslServerAuthenticator.handleSaslToken()` (L474\u2013480):\n```java\n} catch (SaslAuthenticationException e) {\n    buildResponseOnAuthenticateFailure(requestContext,\n            new SaslAuthenticateResponse(...\n                    .setErrorMessage(e.getMessage())));\n    throw e;\n}\n```\nThe exception message is included in the `SASL_AUTHENTICATE` error response. PLAIN throws specific `SaslAuthenticationException` messages:\n- `\"Authentication failed: username not specified\"` \u2014 distinguishes missing username from wrong credentials\n- `\"Authentication failed: password not specified\"` \u2014 distinguishes missing password\n- `\"Authentication failed: Invalid username or password\"` \u2014 returned for bad credentials\n\nThis differentiation between \"field missing\" vs \"wrong credentials\" may provide marginal information to an attacker. By contrast, `SaslException` (non-`SaslAuthenticationException`) messages are stripped to a generic error at line 487\u2013496.\n\n### 9. SCRAM Salt/Iteration Disclosure to Unauthenticated Clients\n\n**Location**: `ScramSaslServer.java:evaluateResponse()` (L135\u2013140)\n\nThe server's `ServerFirstMessage` response (sent before the client proves knowledge of the password) contains the salt and iteration count from the stored `ScramCredential`. This is a protocol requirement of RFC 5802, but it means:\n- Any unauthenticated client can retrieve the salt and iterations for any valid username\n- For invalid usernames, `scramCredential == null` and a `SaslException` is thrown (generic error to client)\n- This reveals a timing/error difference that confirms username existence (though via error, not via successful response)\n\nAdditionally, SCRAM-SHA-256 with low iteration counts (stored in the credential) weakens the offline attack difficulty. The code enforces `scramCredential.iterations() >= mechanism.minIterations()` (L133\u2013134), which is a positive control.\n\n### 10. SCRAM Credential Cache Populated from Metadata\n\n`ScramServerCallbackHandler` reads from `CredentialCache.Cache<ScramCredential>` which is populated by the broker from ZooKeeper (legacy) or KRaft metadata. The stored `ScramCredential` contains `salt`, `iterations`, `serverKey` (HMAC-SHA256(StoredKey, \"Server Key\")), and `storedKey` (H(ClientKey)). Plaintext passwords are never stored or transmitted. This is a strong design.\n\n### 11. Re-Authentication Principal Pinning (Positive Mitigation)\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.java:reauthInfo.ensurePrincipalUnchanged()` (L642\u2013648) enforces that re-authentication must complete with the same principal as the original authentication. A client cannot use re-authentication to escalate to a different identity on the same TCP connection.\n\n### 12. Mechanism Name Validation (Positive Mitigation)\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleHandshakeRequest()` (L554) validates the client-requested mechanism against `enabledMechanisms` (populated from server config). A client cannot request an unexpected mechanism.\n\n### 13. Error Message Scrubbing for SaslException (Positive Mitigation)\n\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.java:handleSaslToken()` (L487\u2013496) strips `SaslException` (non-authentication exceptions) to a generic message before sending to client: `\"Authentication failed during authentication due to invalid credentials with SASL mechanism PLAIN\"`. This prevents internal exception details from leaking.\n\n### 14. KafkaPrincipal Name Directly from SASL Authorization ID\n\nThe `KafkaPrincipal.name` field is set directly from `saslServer.getAuthorizationID()`, which in PLAIN and SCRAM is the client-supplied username (after validation). This means the principal name used for ACL matching is derived from untrusted input that has been authenticated, but not further sanitized or normalized. If an operator creates an ACL for `User:alice` and a client authenticates with `User:ALICE`, they would not match (case-sensitive). This is expected behavior but operators must be aware that principal names are case-sensitive and must exactly match configured ACLs.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kafka SASL authentication flow is architecturally sound: `ChannelBuilders` selects `SaslChannelBuilder` which wires per-mechanism callback handlers to `SaslServerAuthenticator`. The authenticator drives a strict state machine (ApiVersions \u2192 SaslHandshake \u2192 Authenticate \u2192 Complete) and routes SASL tokens to mechanism-specific `SaslServer` implementations. Post-authentication, `KafkaPrincipal` is extracted via `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder` using `SaslServer.getAuthorizationID()` and passed to `Authorizer.authorize()` for ACL enforcement.\n\n**The most significant security findings are:**\n\n1. **Default OAUTHBEARER bypass** (`SaslChannelBuilder.java:330`): The default `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` accepts any JWT without signature verification \u2014 a complete auth bypass unless explicitly overridden.\n\n2. **PLAIN username timing oracle** (`PlainServerCallbackHandler.java:61\u201369`): The constant-time comparison is bypassed for non-existent usernames, enabling timing-based username enumeration.\n\n3. **PLAIN over plaintext transport**: SASL/PLAIN provides zero protection when deployed with `SASL_PLAINTEXT`. Credentials are transmitted as NUL-delimited UTF-8 visible to any network observer.\n\n4. **No brute-force protection**: The SASL layer performs no connection-level or credential-attempt rate limiting.\n\n5. **Optional authorization**: Authentication does not require authorization to be configured; a broker with no `authorizer.class.name` performs no access control on authenticated sessions.\n\n**Recommended remediations:**\n- Explicitly configure `OAuthBearerValidatorCallbackHandler` and JWKS endpoint for production OAUTHBEARER deployments\n- Apply constant-time comparison for the missing-username path in PLAIN (e.g., compare against a dummy password of equal length)\n- Enforce `SASL_SSL` for PLAIN; document and ideally warn at startup if `PLAIN` is enabled on `SASL_PLAINTEXT`\n- Implement broker-side authentication rate limiting (connection throttling per source IP or per username)\n- Warn at startup if no authorizer is configured when authentication mechanisms are enabled\n",
  "path": "/logs/agent/solution.md",
  "security_risk": "LOW"

Here's a summary of what was traced and found:\n\n## What Was Analyzed\n\n### Architecture Chain\n`ChannelBuilders.serverChannelBuilder()` \u2192 `SaslChannelBuilder` (wires callback handlers + JAAS) \u2192 `SaslServerAuthenticator` (state machine) \u2192 mechanism-specific `SaslServer` \u2192 `KafkaPrincipal` \u2192 `Authorizer.authorize()`\n\n### SASL Handshake Protocol\nThe server-side state machine enforces: `INITIAL_REQUEST` \u2192 `ApiVersionsRequest` (optional) \u2192 `SaslHandshakeRequest` (mechanism negotiation) \u2192 `AUTHENTICATE` (token exchange) \u2192 `COMPLETE`. Mechanism names from clients are validated against the server's `sasl.enabled.mechanisms` whitelist.\n\n### PLAIN Mechanism\n- `PlainSaslServer.evaluateResponse()` parses NUL-delimited UTF-8 (authzid/username/password)\n- `PlainServerCallbackHandler.authenticate()` looks up `user_<username>` from JAAS config\n- Uses `Utils.isEqualConstantTime()` for password comparison\n\n### SCRAM Mechanism\n- Two-round exchange: ClientFirst (username + nonce) \u2192 ServerFirst (salt + iterations) \u2192 ClientFinal (proof) \u2192 ServerFinal (server signature)\n- `ScramServerCallbackHandler` fetches `ScramCredential` from `CredentialCache` by client-supplied username\n- Proof verified via `MessageDigest.isEqual()` (constant-time)\n\n### KafkaPrincipal Extraction\n`SaslServerAuthenticator.principal()` \u2192 `DefaultKafkaPrincipalBuilder.build(SaslAuthenticationContext)` \u2192 `new KafkaPrincipal(\"User\", saslServer.getAuthorizationID())` \u2014 the authorization ID from the SASL exchange becomes the principal name for ACL matching.\n\n## Key Security Findings\n\n1. **Default OAUTHBEARER bypass** \u2014 `OAuthBearerUnsecuredValidatorCallbackHandler` is the default when no callback class is explicitly configured; it accepts any JWT without cryptographic validation (complete auth bypass)\n2. **PLAIN username timing oracle** \u2014 constant-time comparison is skipped when username doesn't exist in JAAS config, enabling username enumeration via timing\n3. **PLAIN cleartext over SASL_PLAINTEXT** \u2014 credentials transmitted unprotected if TLS is not used\n4. **No brute-force protection** \u2014 no rate limiting or lockout at the SASL layer\n5. **Optional authorization** \u2014 no `authorizer.class.name` = no access control despite successful authentication\n6. **PLAIN exception message leakage** \u2014 `SaslAuthenticationException` messages (distinguishing \"username not specified\" vs \"invalid credentials\") are sent to clients"
